<div id="review_756600402" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756600402" />
    <a title="Sheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7300331-sheri"><img alt="Sheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378517294p2/7300331.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756600402?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheri" href="/user/show/7300331-sheri">Sheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7300331-sheri?shelf=tragically-beautiful">tragically-beautiful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756600402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2822377268933105903">The song of this story is gorgeous. <br/>It flows beyond the pages and touches you; leaving you forever changed. <br/>My heart is full...my heart is happy...my heart now contains pieces of Skylar and his world. <br/>I believe a Native American proverb pulls my thoughts together nicely….<br/><blockquote>
  <i> “There is a battle of two wolves inside us all.<br/>One is evil. <br/>It is anger, jealously, greed, resentment, lies, inferiority and ego.<br/>The other is good. <br/>It is joy, peace, love, hope, humility, kindness, empathy and truth.<br/>The wolf</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2822377268933105903" style="display:none">The song of this story is gorgeous. <br>It flows beyond the pages and touches you; leaving you forever changed. <br>My heart is full...my heart is happy...my heart now contains pieces of Skylar and his world. <br>I believe a Native American proverb pulls my thoughts together nicely….<br><blockquote>
  <i> “There is a battle of two wolves inside us all.<br>One is evil. <br>It is anger, jealously, greed, resentment, lies, inferiority and ego.<br>The other is good. <br>It is joy, peace, love, hope, humility, kindness, empathy and truth.<br>The wolf that wins? The one you feed.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Skylar is not only the epitome of the good wolf, but he stirs the good wolf inside me.</b> I was overcome with peace and love listening to Skylar’s story. He made me want to be better...be more. He may not be able to speak, but his voice is probably the most powerful I’ve ever read.<br><br>The characters absolutely <i>made</i> this book. I fell head over heels for Skylar and I adore Rafael nearly as much. The beautiful flow of Christo's words transported me to the Reserve. Brilliant writing!<br>The blurb is clear and accurate. <br>Skylar is the sun and Rafael is the wildflower...and together they grow, bloom and thrive in each other's presence. It was calm, serene and soothing despite the ugly shadows lingering from the past. Shocking and disturbing secrets are revealed and I fought the urge, the<b> need</b>, to comfort and hug Sky. A boy with more heartache than anyone should endure, yet somehow he continues to brighten the world around him. His name is fitting, for he shines and he seems to enrich everything he touches. <br>From tattoos...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395064045i/8941978.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>to sun-catchers...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395064045i/8941979.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>...I was spellbound.<br><br>~The writing is dazzling- creating vivid pictures of the Native American culture.<br>~The characters are exceptional, intoxicating and despite their flaws, lovable.<br>~The story that unfolds is touching, unforgettable, and heart-warming.<br><br>A beautiful coming-of-age tale blended with friends to ‘more-than-friends’ and self-discovery and acceptance.<br>Overall, I believe it is truly an epic love story of the balance between light and dark and the miraculous power of compassion and pure love.<br><br><b>*4.5 <i>forever-in-my-heart</i> stars*</b><br><br>Stop by <a href="http://boysinourbooks.com/2014/03/17/group-challenge-review-giveaway-gives-light-by-rose-christo/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Boys in Our Books</b>
</a> to check out our group challenge <b>and</b> a chance to win the<b> ENTIRE</b> <i>'Gives Light'</i> series...<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380435209i/879238.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2816001147461927121"><br/>If I have to describe this book just in a few words I'd chose<br/><br/><i>beautiful</i><br/><br/><i>quiet</i><br/><br/><i>warm</i><br/><br/><i>poignant</i><br/><br/>and <i>sweet</i>.<br/><br/>It's a YA book but it is one of those books I'd recommended even as a family reading in front of a fireplace, yes, for a whole family, because there is so much heart and soul in this book; there is nothing forbidden dark or melodramatic here; there are no any sexual excesses in it. <br/><br/>The heart-warming book tells in a very poetical way the story of of Skylar, a half white/half Native American 16 years o</span>
  <span id="freeText2816001147461927121" style="display:none"><br />If I have to describe this book just in a few words I'd chose<br /><br /><i>beautiful</i><br /><br /><i>quiet</i><br /><br /><i>warm</i><br /><br /><i>poignant</i><br /><br />and <i>sweet</i>.<br /><br />It's a YA book but it is one of those books I'd recommended even as a family reading in front of a fireplace, yes, for a whole family, because there is so much heart and soul in this book; there is nothing forbidden dark or melodramatic here; there are no any sexual excesses in it. <br /><br />The heart-warming book tells in a very poetical way the story of of Skylar, a half white/half Native American 16 years old boy who has to come back to the place of his birth, in the Shoshone Nettlebush reservation, because his farther disappeared. <br />This reunion with his past will change his life.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Gives Light</i>
</b> is about friendship,trust, lost, love and...life how it is- unpredictable, tragical, intense and... grateful...<br /><br />Amazingly written! <br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_420937996" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420937996" />
    <a title="Bookwatcher " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3389262-bookwatcher"><img alt="Bookwatcher " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327517258p2/3389262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420937996?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwatcher " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwatcher " href="/user/show/3389262-bookwatcher">Bookwatcher </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bookwatcher  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4410381-fiona-goodman">Fiona Goodman</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3389262-bookwatcher?shelf=disability">disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3389262-bookwatcher?shelf=glbt-gay">glbt-gay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3389262-bookwatcher?shelf=teen-ya">teen-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420937996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11771341935805158987"><blockquote>
<b>no voice, but certainly he has a lot to say...</b>. That's the better line I can find to describe the main character of this story, Skylar<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392229i/755126.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><b>Blurb</b><br/>Sixteen old boy, alone and voiceless. How you feel if you where him, Skylar? The book begin with this only man, abandoned by his father and took to his grandmother house.<br/>Sky is not just a teenager. A surviver from a brutal crime, that left him with useless vocal cords, and a dead mother, he is also a Native American by blood, his father is Shoshone. His sto</span>
  <span id="freeText11771341935805158987" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<b>no voice, but certainly he has a lot to say...</b>. That's the better line I can find to describe the main character of this story, Skylar<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392229i/755126.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><br><b>Blurb</b><br>Sixteen old boy, alone and voiceless. How you feel if you where him, Skylar? The book begin with this only man, abandoned by his father and took to his grandmother house.<br>Sky is not just a teenager. A surviver from a brutal crime, that left him with useless vocal cords, and a dead mother, he is also a Native American by blood, his father is Shoshone. His story is the voice of someone that don't know much about his family traditions and the way of live in the Shoshone reservation.<br><br><b>What is the best quality of this book?</b><br>In my modest opinion all the information about the native americans. Sky will learn and tell you everything about his father's tribe (his mother is not a Native American) but also start to see and learn about many other tribe. Each pauwow he will learn more about other reservations, and of course also you. It's mesmerizing... I love each story, each character and their unique traditions.<br><br><b>It's a young-adult story?</b><br>I think so, but I prefer to classify it a "for everyone" not just YA story. Certainly it's also a romance, because Sky will meet a boy and start a deep friendship with him. His name is Rafael, and what an irony... Sky best friend and possible his biggest crush, is the son of the serial killer that destroyed his family. I said "possible" crush, I know. He is young, he is starting to discover his origins, but also starting to understand he maybe be in love with Rafael. I will not spoil saying more, you must read to know.<br><br><b>There is also some activism or it's just a 5 stars nonfiction book?</b><br>Oh yeah, definitively this book is much more than just a boys story.<br>There is a bitter message too, of how Native American are saw, and treated.<br>Each time the main character will be frustrated, seeing the injustice and prejudice you will be frustrated too. Each time he will be mad, you will want to go, hug him and tell everything will change... but maybe it's not that easy.<br>I don't know particulars about Native Americans... I never even travel to USA.. what I know is what I read/saw online/watch in movies. So yeah, I'm very ignorant in this topic... but I know... I really know (for my own personal experience) how you feel after a racist comment, a hate stare, just because you are you.<br>I can't say if all the Native American information is this book is precise or not. It help me to know more? I will certainly answer <b>YES</b>. <br><br><b>This is a Native American tale, from a boy that happen to be also gay</b><br>Don't fool yourself reading it just because of the LGBT theme. It's really not the main focus of the story.<br><br>This is a story of a voiceless young boy, that represent many other voiceless Native American fighting for their rights to be... themselves.<br><br><b>I recommend it to readers with open mind. Don't read it thinking it will a boring lesson about Indians</b>. It's a very funny story (Sky is really a very funny boy!), with interesting tales... but also a little activism... to pass you a message of equality and human rights... Yeah human not civil rights, that should be applied to everyone, despite of all races, colors, sexual orientation and creeds.... because it's what we all are, humans.<br><br><b>5 stars</b><br><br><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11771341935805158987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8110617-ilhem?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8110617-ilhem?shelf=sid-love">sid-love</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443255614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17003923742587941797"><br/><br/>This story is about Skylar Saint Clair whose laughs are soundless and who speaks with his smiles, who’s cheeky and open-hearted; about Rafael Gives Light, whose father <i>”liked hurting women”</i>, who draws gifts for the dead, who’s fierce and protective, and can read Skylar’s face. It’s about them gaining something beautiful and positive out of something ugly and terrifying.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>”[…] Rafael pushed me up against the wall and kissed me, hard and wanting and fierce, filled to the brim with emotions that s</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText17003923742587941797" style="display:none"><br /><br />This story is about Skylar Saint Clair whose laughs are soundless and who speaks with his smiles, who’s cheeky and open-hearted; about Rafael Gives Light, whose father <i>”liked hurting women”</i>, who draws gifts for the dead, who’s fierce and protective, and can read Skylar’s face. It’s about them gaining something beautiful and positive out of something ugly and terrifying.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>”[…] Rafael pushed me up against the wall and kissed me, hard and wanting and fierce, filled to the brim with emotions that spilled other, and I held him close, and anchored him to me, anchoring him to earth.”</i>
</b><br /><br />From serial killer’s victim and son, they become buddies, boyfriends and members of a pack of friends, they bring each other solace and balance, and are on their way of finding their place in a world they’re attuned to.<br /><br />I agree with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/443200206 " rel="nofollow noopener">Elizabetta</a> that the author’s voice took precedence over her character’s, there were moments when I longed for Rafael’s POV, for duality and excitement; it is a little one-sided too. I loved it and fell for Skylar and Rafael all the same.<br /><br />“Gives Light” is a lovely story that speaks of the Plains people and of harmony.<br /><br /><i>This was a buddy read with Elizabetta for <a href="http://sidlove.wordpress.com/ " rel="nofollow noopener">The Blog of Sid Love</a><br /></i></span>

<div id="review_634048288" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/634048288" />
    <a title="Jenni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9517353-jenni"><img alt="Jenni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547827038p2/9517353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/634048288?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenni" href="/user/show/9517353-jenni">Jenni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9517353-jenni?shelf=biob">biob</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9517353-jenni?shelf=makes-my-heart-flutter">makes-my-heart-flutter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9517353-jenni?shelf=series-love">series-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9517353-jenni?shelf=sticky-sweet">sticky-sweet</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9517353-jenni?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9517353-jenni?shelf=ya-na">ya-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9517353-jenni?shelf=comfort-food">comfort-food</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634048288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2186039784561780581">Maybe it’s a weird thing to say in a review about a book I chose to read, but here goes. I feel grateful for having experienced <i>Gives Light</i>. This book was one of the most unassuming, comforting novels I've read in quite a long time. It’s one of those books that sits quietly, patiently on your shelf, and once you've read the last page, you wonder how in the world you waited so long to start. <br/><br/>If you asked me to describe it in just <b>one</b> word, out of <b>ALL</b> the words, I could tell you instantly, and wit</span>
  <span id="freeText2186039784561780581" style="display:none">Maybe it’s a weird thing to say in a review about a book I chose to read, but here goes. I feel grateful for having experienced <i>Gives Light</i>. This book was one of the most unassuming, comforting novels I've read in quite a long time. It’s one of those books that sits quietly, patiently on your shelf, and once you've read the last page, you wonder how in the world you waited so long to start. <br><br>If you asked me to describe it in just <b>one</b> word, out of <b>ALL</b> the words, I could tell you instantly, and without hesitation. Reading <i>Gives Light</i> left me with an overwhelming sense of...<i>quiet</i>. It’s a story of both losing and finding yourself. It’s a story of forgiveness, redemption, family, heart, love. <br><br>It’s about talking without speaking—literally and figuratively. There’s mystery. There’s fight, there’s beauty. No words are wasted, every word paints a picture. <br><br>From Skylar’s father (and mother) to Granny to Annie, to Raf’s father and every single, solitary character in between, there’s magic. <br><br>I’m not going to pretend I’m something I’m not. I like heat and intimacy in my books. I don’t need it to be gratuitous, I just want it there. Of course in YA, and well, any other book, sometimes that magic happens off the page. Sometimes it works, a lot of times it doesn't. Not so with <i>Gives Light</i>. I felt so much intimacy between Sky and Raf. They’re clearly in love, they clearly enjoy giving and showing affection. And I felt it, in what wasn't there, and it was beautiful. It came through in the smallest of ways, and if you don’t pay attention, maybe you’ll miss out. When Raf gives Sky the plains flute, the way Raf knows what Sky is feeling and thinking. It's the things *not* done or said that bring so much feeling into the story. The intimacy...<i>unf</i>. <br><br>Listen, I could go on and on and on, or my review could be these four words alone: <b>I loved this book</b>. I’ll leave it at that for now. <br><br>If you haven’t already, you should read <i>Gives Light</i>. The sooner the better. As for me, I can’t wait to experience the rest of the series; I won’t wait long, that’s for sure.<br><br>I read <i>Gives Light</i> as part of a BioB team challenge. Check out our group review, plus enter to win <b>all four books</b> (LUCKY YOU!) in the series by clicking <a href="http://boysinourbooks.com/2014/03/17/group-challenge-review-giveaway-gives-light-by-rose-christo/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. <br><br><a href="http://boysinourbooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387293005i/7570780.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> </span>

<div id="review_443092046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/443092046" />
    <a title="ttg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1629211-ttg"><img alt="ttg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360462250p2/1629211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/443092046?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ttg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ttg" href="/user/show/1629211-ttg">ttg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1629211-ttg?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1629211-ttg?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1629211-ttg?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1629211-ttg?shelf=challenge-read">challenge-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443092046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8089915892343706011">Gives Light is a like a long walk in the woods. It’s not an overly tense, angsty, or action-packed book. It’s a quiet, thoughtful, and meaningful coming-of-age story with a sweet YA-level romance between two teens, the son of a murder victim and the son of the murderer.<br/><br/>The story is told by sixteen-year old Skylar, whose throat was cut when he was five by the same man who killed his mother. Skylar survived, but lost his voice. After the attack, his father packed him up and they left the Shoshone </span>
  <span id="freeText8089915892343706011" style="display:none">Gives Light is a like a long walk in the woods. It’s not an overly tense, angsty, or action-packed book. It’s a quiet, thoughtful, and meaningful coming-of-age story with a sweet YA-level romance between two teens, the son of a murder victim and the son of the murderer.<br /><br />The story is told by sixteen-year old Skylar, whose throat was cut when he was five by the same man who killed his mother. Skylar survived, but lost his voice. After the attack, his father packed him up and they left the Shoshone Indian reservation where they had lived all his life. Eleven years later, Skylar’s dad goes missing, and he’s returned to the reservation to live with a grandmother he does not remember, and a culture that now seems alien.<br /><br />But even with the worries about his missing father, Skylar is an upbeat presence, and he takes in his new home with his usual curiosity and easy, accepting nature. And soon, he makes friends, learns more about his Shoshone background, and is drawn to a moody, passionate young man, a young man who shares a similar face to one he remembers from a dark night so long ago.<br /><br />Gives Light might sound dark and angsty, but it’s not. The murders in the past are kind of heavy in the background, but the real story is about the survivors of those events, how they grieve, move on, accept, forgive, or honor, and about two people finding a much deeper connection of trust and love. It’s also a story about Skylar’s own personal growth and acceptance of himself, including the vicious scars that lance across his neck. <br /><br />There are threads of tension throughout--the mystery around Skylar’s dad, the uneasiness over the sudden appearance of the FBI on the reservation, Skylar’s worries about being removed from his new home, and his confusion over his growing feelings for Raphael. But like the rest of the story, these threads are tied up calmly and quietly, and very meaningfully.<br /><br />It was very good story, and would sit well on any YA LGBT shelf. (No sex--just the safe lovey, kissy stuff.) The growing love story within is very sweet and romantic, and is that kind where you find a lot of satisfaction from just a squeeze of a hand or a kiss on the palm.<br /><br />If you’re up for a quiet, thoughtful read, and are fine with something more YA, than I would recommend this book. It’s self-published, and there were a few editing errors, but nothing that I couldn’t easily overlook. Overall, I thought the writing was very good, and I liked seeing the world through Skylar’s POV; he’s often very adept at reading others, even if he’s sometimes challenged with communicating with them. This is the first book in a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/85919-gives-light" rel="nofollow noopener">four-part series</a>, and I’m definitely looking forward to checking out the next one. <br /><br />As an extra bonus, the full 300+ page novel was $3 for the ebook, which I thought was a good deal for such a nice read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8089915892343706011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_698892555" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698892555" />
    <a title="Sara " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5058304-sara"><img alt="Sara " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439650883p2/5058304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/698892555?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara " href="/user/show/5058304-sara">Sara </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=boys-who-love-boys">boys-who-love-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=debut-read-from-new-to-me-author">debut-read-from-new-to-me-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=can-t-miss-book">can-t-miss-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=goo-is-good">goo-is-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=stellar">stellar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=kleenex-worthy">kleenex-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=biob">biob</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698892555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14710583269592868402"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I was very unsure about reading this book. I mean, I wanted to and it had been on my TBR list for some time but I am hesitant when books contain actual history in them. I am afraid that it will be too much to take or that it will be so technical that it will go over my head at the speed of sound and I will miss the point entirely. Thank goodness, Gives Light and Rose Christo did NOT do that to me. <br/><br/>So this book, I am at a loss of words with how to describe it. I am not being cheeky with </span>
  <span id="freeText14710583269592868402" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>I was very unsure about reading this book. I mean, I wanted to and it had been on my TBR list for some time but I am hesitant when books contain actual history in them. I am afraid that it will be too much to take or that it will be so technical that it will go over my head at the speed of sound and I will miss the point entirely. Thank goodness, Gives Light and Rose Christo did NOT do that to me. <br><br>So this book, I am at a loss of words with how to describe it. I am not being cheeky with the loss of words and Skylar being mute, I just do not know how to get out what this book did to me. It was transcendent. There is an SAT word for you. I was blown away by the powerful voice given to a young man who has lost his ability to speak. Skylar St. Clair was an amazing character to read. He is one of my favorites in the YA genre and along with Skylar I have to add into that favorite list Rafael. Oh boys, you killed me with your story. <br><br>Writing this review is giving me the chills, in a good way of course, but going over my notes and highlights all the feelings are coming back in a rush. From Skylar’s first communication about his father being missing to meeting his grandmother on the Nettlebush reservation for the first time and when he looks over at dinner into eyes he swears he has seen before…*shivers* This book had me on my butt, I will tell you that. I am in awe of what I have read. I am so happy that the challenge was made and I was given that push to read this, to finally have the beauty that Gives Light shone upon me and feel it down to my core. Does that sound really mushy? Oh well. This book makes me want to write poetry to it. It makes me want to be a better person because I read it. It…it just makes me feel more than I can comprehend. <br><br>Oh and it made me look up bugs…me and bugs are not friends at all but I was looking up bugs. How is that possible? It made me look up bugs and it transported me from a baseball field for Little League Opening Ceremonies and had me on the Nettlebush reservation feeling the same about animals as Skylar did. We have that bit in common. It just moved me. That is all. It moved me. <br><br>I won’t go into depth about the story. But I will say that the relationships in this book are gorgeous. Not only is the love story of Skylar and Rafael one of the best I have read in YA but Skylar’s relationship with Annie, his father, Granny and most of all the reservation and his culture. It was outstanding. I learned so much right along with Skylar about his heritage and I just learned so much about the human condition. The way we can turn situations into what we need; the way we can take something that is utterly awful and see beyond the ugly to what is there and love it. Oh I am getting lost. I think it’s time to wrap this baby up and hug it again. <br><br>Gives Light is an amazing story. Even if you are fickle about the YA genre, this will prove that even books without sex on the page can be the most intimate thing you will ever read. This story was one I couldn’t let end when I read the last word on the last page, I immediately started book 2 and am halfway through the last book in the series. It’s rare for me to do that; read an author back to back or continue a series that way but I couldn’t let Skylar and Rafael go that soon. I had to keep reading and though their story will end, it is not one that will leave me anytime soon. How can it? <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The more he talked, the more I listened. The more I listened, the more I forgot that I wasn’t talking back. I could scratch my chin or quirk my eyebrows or tilt my head and he knew exactly what the gesture meant. He knew what I was feeling, if not what I was thinking. He made me feel like I had a voice. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><i>Gives Light was read as a challenge with the girls From <b>Boys in our Books</b>. You can see our reactions and enter to win all four books from this series here: <br><br></i><p>
  <a href="http://boysinourbooks.com/2014/03/17/group-challenge-review-giveaway-gives-light-by-rose-christo/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="GRBannersubtext" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395016028i/8935848.jpg" width="300" height="121" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p></span>

<div id="review_420292092" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420292092" />
    <a title="Irina Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena"><img alt="Irina Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587303756p2/7664770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420292092?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irina Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irina Elena" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena">Irina Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781311662491" href="/book/show/16120803-gives-light">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=ya-realistic">ya-realistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=disabilities-disorders-and-diseases">disabilities-disorders-and-diseases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=crime-thriller-mystery-suspense">crime-thriller-mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420292092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14253740967380469181">Here's one thing that's going to tell you a lot about this book and the effect it has on people: writing a very positive review about it instead of full-on gushing is going to make me the odd one out, the meanie and the heartless critic.<br/>So be it - I feel it is my duty to the people of GR to point out all I found was wrong with this book. But don't worry, there isn't that much stuff to criticise. (Or: there is, but it doesn't weigh in on my final opinion that much, strangely.)<br/><br/>Due to the aforement</span>
  <span id="freeText14253740967380469181" style="display:none">Here's one thing that's going to tell you a lot about this book and the effect it has on people: writing a very positive review about it instead of full-on gushing is going to make me the odd one out, the meanie and the heartless critic.<br />So be it - I feel it is my duty to the people of GR to point out all I found was wrong with this book. But don't worry, there isn't that much stuff to criticise. (Or: there is, but it doesn't weigh in on my final opinion that much, strangely.)<br /><br />Due to the aforementioned gushing, I expected to be blown out of the water, and I think that may have been part of the reason why I felt a little let down when I started reading.<br />The writing is decent, but once in a while a particularly awkward sentence suddenly jarred me out of the story. The dialogue is fine, as long as you don't try to picture teenagers actually talking the way they do here. (I would know.)<br />The relationship development is absurdly quick. As soon as Skylar moves into the reservation, he falls into things in a way that doesn't ring true in the least. The process itself is sudden and unnatural, but this is where I start talking about this story's positives, because once these new relationships are formed, be they between friends or family members, they feel warm and comforting in a way that's hard to convey.<br /><br />The atmosphere that permeates the reservation is absolutely wonderful. Between the cultural aspects, this natural way of living that's completely foreign to me, city girl born and bred, and the way the population is so thick-knitted and close, I never wanted to leave the place Christo was painting in my mind.<br /><br />Sure, I have more to criticise.<br />Rafael and Skylar's personalities are well-rounded and nuanced, but at the same time mildly baffling.<br />Rafael is much more that he initially seems - more tender, shy but unafraid, brooding but down to earth. But there are things about his character that don't make sense. He listens to power metal and goes to the city library, but has never been to the cinema. He draws constantly, but doesn't own coloured pencils (and is shocked and pleased out of his mind when Skylar buys them for him as a gift).<br />Skylar, on the other hand, is non-confrontational in a way that I can't really connect with, but I guess being mute will do that to you, so I'm just going to roll with it. What I'm not going to roll with is the fact that he keeps swear jars, because he's a goddamn high-schooler who's been to public school his whole life, and I can assure you: his brain cannot work like that, so spare me.<br />The main issue - the crime/mystery core of the book - is slightly surreal, and the ending is more than slightly anticlimactic. Furthermore, a minor issue that has the potential to wreak havoc in Skylar's mind and family is completely forgotten after the first time it's mentioned (because I guess that's easier).<br /><br />And still, despite all the things I have to bitch about, this book sucked me in in a hot second, because its characters are sympathetic and original and its setting is fascinating to say the least.<br />The tone of the storytelling makes it feel more cosy than heartwrenching - a slow, aching journey, but not one devoid of beauty and joy. Watching it unfold and soaking in the atmosphere had a strangely calming effect on me that very few things have.<br />It's a sweet, heartwarming and hopeful story, with a hint of mystery to keep things exciting, and I can definitely see how it managed to charm even callous, cold-hearted YA haters like Tinka.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14253740967380469181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_868231730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/868231730" />
    <a title="Ami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/134600-ami"><img alt="Ami" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485783876p2/134600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/868231730?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ami" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ami" href="/user/show/134600-ami">Ami</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ami by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/739211-susan">Susan</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=4-and-half-stars_rating">4-and-half-stars_rating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=mm-young-or-new-adult">mm-young-or-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=new-to-me-authors-2014">new-to-me-authors-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=new-to-me-mm-authors-2014">new-to-me-mm-authors-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer868231730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer660533898040395116">This has been a <a href='http://boysinourbooks.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Boys in Our Books Group</a> Challenge.<br/><br/>For complete group review: <b>
  <a href='boysinourbooks.com/2014/03/17/group-challenge-review-giveaway-gives-light-by-rose-christo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Please Click Here</a>
</b><br/><br/>------<br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I couldn't possibly put into words what that meant to me. Nor had I realized until that moment how much of a group project it was to grow up. Each of us is just an imprint of the many people who have crossed paths with us over the years, some more times than others. Most of us never think to say thank you. I know I never had."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Rose Christo's "<b>Gives Light</b>" is like calm water. There</span>
  <span id="freeText660533898040395116" style="display:none">This has been a <a href="http://boysinourbooks.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Boys in Our Books Group</a> Challenge.<br><br>For complete group review: <b>
  <a href="boysinourbooks.com/2014/03/17/group-challenge-review-giveaway-gives-light-by-rose-christo" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Click Here</a>
</b><br><br>------<br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I couldn't possibly put into words what that meant to me. Nor had I realized until that moment how much of a group project it was to grow up. Each of us is just an imprint of the many people who have crossed paths with us over the years, some more times than others. Most of us never think to say thank you. I know I never had."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Rose Christo's "<b>Gives Light</b>" is like calm water. There is something soothing when you read the words, like a soft blanket, covering you, making you feel relaxed and safe. It might have to do with the setting -- everything happens inside an Indian reservation, so in a way, it makes everyone protected from the outside world. Even state laws don't apply to reservations.<br><br>It might also have to do with Skylar -- being mute after a tragedy that takes away his mother's life; you are conditioned to see the world from his other senses. How he sees things, how he absorbs things, how he makes sense of what happens around him. I love Skylar ... even if sometimes he seems younger than he actually is, but his ingenuity wins him over. He is like a new gentle soul -- I love being inside his mind. I love his soundless laughter the most though.<br><br>The story moves naturally, in a gentle way; never pushy, never forced. The relationship between Rafael and Skylar feels natural; the connection between them magical yet believable. While I adore Skylar for his innocence, I love Rafael for being fierce and determined and loyal ("I won't let them," Rafael said. "I won't let anyone take you away. I won't let anyone hurt you. I'll protect you. I'll always protect you. I don't care how. I just will."). There are just SO MANY FEELS in this book and I keep feeling like my heart is going up my throat.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Time, at some point, became inconsequential. Time wasn't Rafael; time didn't matter. Only Rafael mattered. Only Rafael possessed my thoughts, my every pounding pulse, euphoric and bittersweet, illogical and wonderful. For that moment, devoid of time, even I didn't exist, except for the part of me that was touching Rafael, kissing Rafael, the part of me that couldn't tell where Rafael ended and I began."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I fall in love with all the characters. Even if the story is written from Sky's perspective, I can feel everyone's personality just fine. From Sky's other friends: Annie, Aubrey, Lila, Joseph ... to his Grandma (I love that woman!) to his father (when he said "Skylar," he said. "I love you," he repeated. "I love you," he said once more. "No matter who you love." -- I just MELT right there). Even Nola Red Clay, whom for a moment, makes me admire lawyers *lol*.<br><br>The book is not perfect though, which is why I can only give it 4.5 stars. I admit that there are times I wish for ripples to shake up things. The problem with Sky's father, for example, I wish it has been explored more rather than being written near the end, like a rushed resolution. So yes, I get "my ripples", but I can understand why for some, this could feel boring.<br><br>Nonetheless, this has been a lovely read. Definitely one of the most satisfying reads this year ...<br><br><br><br><a href="http://boysinourbooks.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427601i/854880.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="660533898040395116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_420122270" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420122270" />
    <a title="Nikyta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2669008-nikyta"><img alt="Nikyta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584238083p2/2669008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420122270?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikyta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikyta" href="/user/show/2669008-nikyta">Nikyta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=broken-to-bits">broken-to-bits</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=stayed-up-all-night-to-read">stayed-up-all-night-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=all-time-favs">all-time-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=little-or-no-smexing">little-or-no-smexing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=bubbles-safe">bubbles-safe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=disability">disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=series-serial">series-serial</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=in-sickness-and-in-health">in-sickness-and-in-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2669008-nikyta?shelf=want-pbhc">want-pbhc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420122270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1636301020218904092">How exactly am I supposed to review this book? To be honest, I have no freaking idea. It was a phenomenal story. Not exactly something I was expecting (because really, how much stuff can a mute 16 year old get into?) but I fell in love with the story, its characters and their troubles. I even cried once... Okay, maybe it was twice.<br/><br/>Even though Skylar can't talk, he's still a rather chatty boy inside his head. I found that very amusing. He had a sarcastic or funny thought about almost everything w</span>
  <span id="freeText1636301020218904092" style="display:none">How exactly am I supposed to review this book? To be honest, I have no freaking idea. It was a phenomenal story. Not exactly something I was expecting (because really, how much stuff can a mute 16 year old get into?) but I fell in love with the story, its characters and their troubles. I even cried once... Okay, maybe it was twice.<br /><br />Even though Skylar can't talk, he's still a rather chatty boy inside his head. I found that very amusing. He had a sarcastic or funny thought about almost everything within the story. His transition from living in the city to living on the reservation was very well done and how he grows from a timid but angry boy to an accepted and cherished individual was a great thing to watch. More than that, I adored Granny and her role in helping Skylar become a confident, loveable person. Rafael, though, might be my favorite character. I adore Skylar but there's something about those guys who hate the world that get me every time. I loved the way Rafael was able to understand Skylar even though Skylar couldn't talk. He gave Skylar a voice, even if he still couldn't speak. No one understood Rafael until Skylar came along and made it possible for someone to see just how big his heart is. These two together are so sweet and adorable it just about broke my heart. They didn't care that they were supposed to be enemies. Instead, they embraced the connection that is so obvious between them.<br /><br />A big part of the story is the problems reservations go through and how the government treats them. This is actually the theme that the whole series follows. This particular book, though, is focused on the culture of the Shoshone but also the conflict that came out of Skylar's dad conducting a right he was due and the consequences associated with it. Those consequences bleed over to Skylar's new life and starts to cause him and his Granny some trouble. I actually don't want to go into too much detail about these events (I know I'm not doing it justice) because I want the reader to figure them out for themselves. I will say that while the story isn't exactly dark, I felt like there were dark elements within the story. It gave the book depth and emotion because of the problems of the past. The only thing with this story was that it left a few questions unanswered BUT those questions are answered in book two, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15852498.Looks_Over__Gives_Light___2_" title="Looks Over (Gives Light, #2) by Rose Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">Looks Over</a>, so just be patient LOL.<br /><br />All in all, a beautiful story about love, anger and ultimately forgiveness. There are some harsh realities in this series, which made me open my eyes to some things, but it is a very engaging and captivating read. I immediately went onto the second book and then the third book. It's been so long since I found a series I could get so engrossed in but this is definitely one I'll recommend to anyone looking for an exceptionally delightful and alluring read.<br /><br />Be warned, though, this is m/m YA but they are 16 and 17 years old. So if you have issues with minor characters, please do not read this series, you will only be doing it an injustice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1636301020218904092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/441395771?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandapanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandapanda" href="/user/show/3673972-mandapanda">Mandapanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3673972-mandapanda?shelf=various-romance">various-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3673972-mandapanda?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441395771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6339913748748826655">Amazing story of Skylar, a 16 year old boy sent back to an Indian Reservation to live with his grandmother after his father disappears. He falls in love with the boy whose father murdered Skylar's mother.<br/><br/>I couldn't put this book down from the first line. It's intense and beautiful at the same time. I was just as enthralled with the mystery plot and the lives of the people on the reservation, as I was with the slow growing romance between Sky and Rafael Gives Light. <br/><br/>I'm not usually a fan of YA bu</span>
  <span id="freeText6339913748748826655" style="display:none">Amazing story of Skylar, a 16 year old boy sent back to an Indian Reservation to live with his grandmother after his father disappears. He falls in love with the boy whose father murdered Skylar's mother.<br /><br />I couldn't put this book down from the first line. It's intense and beautiful at the same time. I was just as enthralled with the mystery plot and the lives of the people on the reservation, as I was with the slow growing romance between Sky and Rafael Gives Light. <br /><br />I'm not usually a fan of YA but this story transcends both the YA and the romance genres. It's brilliant! There are 4 books in the series (great value at only $2.99) so I'm off to read number 2.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6339913748748826655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KpA+v+j0e7LLl3Aa2vF9xjEi5FAAEjHdlZKuRXp7FAK4UrMuv7TjZ1sLkWjxs5IPcNfbeToXsCyfiqmDPPV7xA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XVKAnUaiCNiwyOrrCO+H7qy3DPx9reWDgC57MRuU4A/PkA0MEeKQDSBUC5kjrWgn7UIz1UeoZHKKNnz3XRqPyQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
